region.</span></p></div><div class="QHblV nkdHX mHUQ kvZxL hTosT whbOj " data-testid="prism-byline"><div class="VZTD mLASH OcxMG oJce "><div class="kKfXc ubAkB VZTD rEPuv "><div class="TQPvQ fVlAg data-testid="prism-divider"></div></div></div></div></div><div style="--spacing-top:0px;--spacing-bottom:32px;--spacing-child-top:initial;--spacing-child-bottom:24px;--spacing-firstChild-top:initial;--spacing-firstChild-bottom:24px;--spacing-lastChild-top:initial;--spacing-lastChild-bottom:initial;--spacing-compact-top:24px;--spacing-compact-bottom:32px;--spacing-firstChild-compact-top:initial;--spacing-firstChild-compact-bottom:24px;--spacing-child-compact-top:initial;--spacing-child-compact-bottom:24px;--spacing-lastChild-compact-top:initial;--spacing-lastChild-compact-bottom:initial" bOdfO qXhdi NFNeu UyHES " data-testid="prism-article-body"><div class="FITT_Article_main_group_wrapper VZTD UeCOM jIRH oimqG DjbQm UwdmX Xmrlz ReShI KaJdY lqtkC ssImf HfYhe RTHNs iJVrZ " data-testid="prism-GridContainer"><div class="Kiog kNVGM nvpSA qwdi bmjsw " data-testid="prism-GridRow"><div class="theme-e oBTii mrzah " data-testid="prism-GridColumn" style="--grid-column-span-xxs:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-xs:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-sm:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-md:20;--grid-column-span-lg:16;--grid-column-span-xl:16;--grid-column-span-xxl:14;--grid-column-start-xxs:auto;--grid-column-start-xs:auto;--grid-column-start-sm:auto;--grid-column-start-md:3;--grid-column-start-lg:5;--grid-column-start-xl:5;--grid-column-start-xxl:6"><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao MvWXB TjIXL aGjvy ebVHC ">In the 18th century B.C., a Canaanite palace at Tel Kabri, in what is today northern Israel, was a sight to behold. The enormous building—at 65,000 square feet it was larger than a modern shopping mall—was replete with wall paintings, a fancy banquet hall, and storage rooms packed with more than a hundred enormous jars of spiced wine.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Then, at some point during that century, the palace was suddenly abandoned and left vacant for almost a millennium.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Some 3,700 years later, beginning in 2009, archaeologists digging up the palace were stumped. This beautiful and important building obviously had served as a political center for Canaanites in the region. And it had been renovated shortly before it fell into disuse. So why did its inhabitants flee?</p></div></div></div><div class="NYwzQ vUYNV glxIO ilAoG HPkGR "><div class="natgeo-ad" data-testid="prism-ad-wrapper" data-testid="prism-caption"><div class="HXPPJ barbu yKsXL IzgMt VcHIt uhSzI YGNMU cRAsZ xqMcl QtRul "><span class="hsDdd OOSI GpQCA lZur VlFaz " data-testid="prism-truncate"><span><span class="gtOSm FbbUW tUtYa vOCwz EQwFq yCufu eEak Qmvg nyTIa SRXVc vzLa jgBfc WXDas CiUCW kqbG zrdEG txGfn ygKVe BbezD UOtxr CVfpq xijV soGRS XgdC sEIlf daWqJ "><p>A wave visible in the far wall of a palace room </span></span></span></div><div class="qinlA IpWvx oqZz tylGM lyWxS nWcVF UhTug PPcLh "><span class="gtOSm FbbUW tUtYa vOCwz EQwFq yCufu eEak Qmvg nyTIa SRXVc vzLa jgBfc WXDas CiUCW kqbG zrdEG txGfn ygKVe BbezD UOtxr CVfpq xijV soGRS XgdC sEIlf daWqJ YNujN JGtjI aZFDu rkKLh ">Photograph by Eric H. Cline</span></div></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">The 75-acre site of<a class="zZygg UbGlr iFzkS qdXbA WCDhQ DbOXS tqUtK GpWVU iJYzE " data-testid="prism-linkbase" href="https://www.nationalgeographic.org/article/tel-kabri-project/"> Tel Kabri</a> lies in a tectonically active region, so it would be easy to lay the blame on an earthquake. But the archaeologists were hesitant: Invoking an earthquake felt like an easy way out, like the joke among archaeologists of assigning a “ritual” purpose to artifacts they can’t otherwise explain.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Instead, the Tel Kabri team spent several dig seasons ruling out the possibilities. With support from the <a class="zZygg UbGlr iFzkS qdXbA WCDhQ DbOXS tqUtK GpWVU iJYzE " data-testid="prism-linkbase" href="https://www.nationalgeographic.org/funding-opportunities/grants/">National Geographic Society</a>, they looked for evidence of drought, flood, or other environmental factors that may have driven away the residents. They looked for signs of fire, weapons, or unburied bodies that may have indicated violence or combat. Nada. Zilch.</p><div class="oLzSq QrHMO fnRUo pvsTF EhJPu vPlOC zNYgW OsTsW RMeqy daRVX ISNQ sKyCY eRftA acPPc MENS nFwaT MCnQE mEeeY SmBjI xegrY rPLsU iulOd NIuqO zzscu lzDCc aHUBM IEgzD OjMNy eQqcx SVqKB </span></span></span></div><div class="qinlA IpWvx oqZz tylGM lyWxS nWcVF UhTug PPcLh "><span class="gtOSm FbbUW tUtYa vOCwz EQwFq yCufu eEak Qmvg nyTIa SRXVc vzLa jgBfc WXDas CiUCW kqbG zrdEG txGfn ygKVe BbezD UOtxr CVfpq xijV soGRS XgdC sEIlf daWqJ YNujN JGtjI aZFDu rkKLh ">Photograph by Griffin Aerial Imaging</span></div></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy "><a class="zZygg UbGlr iFzkS qdXbA WCDhQ DbOXS tqUtK GpWVU iJYzE " data-testid="prism-linkbase" href="https://marsci.haifa.ac.il/index.php/en/staff/civi-faculty/168-ayasur">Assaf Yasur Landau</a> of Haifa University, co-director of the excavation and a co-author of<a class="zZygg UbGlr iFzkS qdXbA WCDhQ DbOXS tqUtK GpWVU iJYzE " data-testid="prism-linkbase" href="https://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0239079"> a study published today</a> in the journal <i class=" ">PLoS One</i>, said it took him six years to warm to the idea that an earthquake may have destroyed the Canaanite palace.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">“I wanted to make absolutely sure that we dotted every i and crossed every t before we reached such a conclusion,” he says. “It’s super important not to be sensationalist and to do good science. Otherwise it’s really bad for science, as well as for the community we serve.”</p></div></div></div><div class="NYwzQ vUYNV glxIO ilAoG HPkGR "><div class="natgeo-ad" data-testid="prism-ad-wrapper" style="min-width:300px;min-height:250px;transition:min-height 0.3s linear 0s" data-ad-placeholder="true"><div data-box-type="fitt-adbox-fitt-article-inline-box" data-testid="prism-ad"><div class="Ad fitt-article-inline-box  ad-slot  " data-slot-type="fitt-article-inline-box" data-slot-kvps="pos=fitt-article-inline-box"></div></div></div></div><div class="FITT_Article_main_group_wrapper VZTD UeCOM jIRH oimqG DjbQm UwdmX Xmrlz ReShI KaJdY lqtkC ssImf HfYhe RTHNs iJVrZ " data-testid="prism-GridContainer"><div class="Kiog kNVGM nvpSA qwdi bmjsw " data-testid="prism-GridRow"><div class="theme-e oBTii mrzah " data-testid="prism-GridColumn" style="--grid-column-span-xxs:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-xs:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-sm:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-md:20;--grid-column-span-lg:16;--grid-column-span-xl:16;--grid-column-span-xxl:14;--grid-column-start-xxs:auto;--grid-column-start-xs:auto;--grid-column-start-sm:auto;--grid-column-start-md:3;--grid-column-start-lg:5;--grid-column-start-xl:5;--grid-column-start-xxl:6"><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">In 2011 the Tel Kabri team began uncovering a trench that appeared to cut straight through the palace. At first the archaeologists assumed it was modern, perhaps an irrigation channel for the avocado farm that surrounded the site, or maybe it was dug during the 1948 Arab-Israeli war.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">“There was a battle in ’48 right across the road,” says Tel Kabri co-director<a class="zZygg UbGlr iFzkS qdXbA WCDhQ DbOXS tqUtK GpWVU iJYzE " data-testid="prism-linkbase" href="https://anthropology.columbian.gwu.edu/eric-h-cline"> Eric Cline</a> of George Washington University. “In our notes we were calling it a modern tank trench.”</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Yet over the course of several excavation seasons, the archaeologists began to notice features in the palace that didn’t seem quite right. Some walls were slightly offset. Some floors were a little “wavy,” sloped at odd angles, or pockmarked, likely by heavy objects falling from a height.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">By 2019, a hundred feet of the trench had been uncovered, and archaeologists noticed that three courses of a wall from the palace appeared to have fallen into the trench.</p><div class="oLzSq QrHMO GbsKS pvsTF EhJPu vPlOC zNYgW OsTsW AMhAA daRVX ISNQ sKyCY eRftA acPPc ebfE nFwaT MCnQE mEeeY SmBjI xegrY VvTxJ iulOd NIuqO zzscu lzDCc aHUBM hbvnu OjMNy eQqcx SVqKB GQmdz jaoD iShaE ONJdw vrZxD OnRTz gbbfF roDbV kRoBe oMlSS gfNzt oJhud eXZcf zhVlX "><div class="XQpSH zzkIM UtCfs sXthe lyRMG " data-testid="prism-divider"></div><div><section class="Kiog iKqXF CHWlW ZgZTu FlDNH hQfuy feniZ wBpop uAyYK yJYJo OGgqj tQHio PCVZs " data-testid="prism-collection"><header class="mLASH VZTD bhaVx "><div><h2 class="KuBvM RTkZF lFzlq GbVC HkWF exKgG kGyAC SwCrv ">You May Also Like</h2></div></header><div class="liAe uMOq zYIfP pYgZk Mxrkk VZTD lZur TPpRg NoUSU igcMP DtJWr QgBvn DFdlJ QGHKv VuOFc rRTs EwJTR UpiKB sKbok RsAxh msYPt zKjNI SXHxp OaElp halTF KzevM LFuuA xTOeQ jLoop " data-testid="prism-card"><a class="iVcn UbGlr ibBnq qdXbA avodi DbOXS tqUtK GpWVU iJYzE QGHKv HNQqj ICwhc Bkgbl ZLXw kSqqG rEBmF " data-testid="prism-linkbase" href="https://www.nationalgeographic.com/history/history-magazine/article/this-american-indian-metropolis-was-mysteriously-abandoned-archaeologists-want-to-know-why" aria-label="This American Indian metropolis was mysteriously abandoned. Archaeologists want to know why." aria-describedby="ThisAmericanIndianmetags"><div class="hsDdd GpQCA lZur BOsoU YMZw dihEb srtah LmIPo JzlZQ qrShQ iRFVw ZZxEf zHngH jCA-DP TucPs XifJd MWLZF PEVz VbrfA zZsl kjmkg OwbFk QuuaM cBQOR "><div class="GpQCA lZur oVsVV nFtJ GHKp awJgN EuJtJ " data-testid="prism-ratio-frame"><div class="FvQLF iLTd NqeUA UzzHi iWsMV "><picture data-testid="prism-picture"><source media="(max-width: 767px)" srcSet="https://i.natgeofe.com/n/9cea17d0-e49d-4a76-b766-929ff97ef0ef/RSCahokia13_square.jpg?w=195&amp;h=195, https://i.natgeofe.com/n/9cea17d0-e49d-4a76-b766-929ff97ef0ef/RSCahokia13_square.jpg?w=390&amp;h=390 2x"/><source media="(min-width: 768px)" srcSet="https://i.natgeofe.com/n/9cea17d0-e49d-4a76-b766-929ff97ef0ef/RSCahokia13_square.jpg?w=220&amp;h=220, https://i.natgeofe.com/n/9cea17d0-e49d-4a76-b766-929ff97ef0ef/RSCahokia13_square.jpg?w=440&amp;h=440 2x"/><img alt="" class="hsDdd " data-testid="prism-image" draggable="false" src="https://i.natgeofe.com/n/9cea17d0-e49d-4a76-b766-929ff97ef0ef/RSCahokia13_square.jpg"/></picture></div></div></div><div class="QGHKv iVcn avodi rEPuv ICwhc ibBnq Bkgbl ZLXw kSqqG rEBmF "><div class="VZTD rEPuv QXDKT pJYTK " data-testid="prism-meta"><div class="CJAFL gDeX "><div class="mLASH VZTD UeCOM wSnmx ltDkr MjHGf rmiAn vvBSK " id="ThisAmericanIndianmetags"><div class="wXbPV YAJid wPGsL ">HISTORY MAGAZINE</div></div><h2 class="PFoxV eBpQD rcQBv bQtjQ lQUdN GpQCA mAkiF FvMyr WvoqU nPLLM tuAKv " id="ThisAmericanIndianmeheadline">This American Indian metropolis was mysteriously abandoned. Archaeologists want to know why.</h2></div></div></div></a></div><div class="liAe uMOq zYIfP pYgZk Mxrkk VZTD lZur TPpRg NoUSU igcMP DtJWr QgBvn DFdlJ QGHKv VuOFc rRTs EwJTR UpiKB sKbok RsAxh msYPt zKjNI SXHxp OaElp halTF KzevM LFuuA xTOeQ jLoop " data-testid="prism-card"><a class="iVcn UbGlr ibBnq qdXbA avodi DbOXS tqUtK GpWVU iJYzE QGHKv HNQqj ICwhc Bkgbl ZLXw kSqqG rEBmF " data-testid="prism-linkbase" href="https://www.nationalgeographic.com/history/article/this-man-drowned-5000-years-ago-how-do-we-know" aria-label="This man drowned 5,000 years ago. How do we know that?" aria-describedby="Thismandrowned5000yetags"><div class="hsDdd GpQCA lZur BOsoU YMZw dihEb srtah LmIPo JzlZQ qrShQ iRFVw ZZxEf zHngH jCA-DP TucPs XifJd MWLZF PEVz VbrfA zZsl kjmkg OwbFk QuuaM cBQOR "><div class="GpQCA lZur oVsVV nFtJ GHKp awJgN EuJtJ " data-testid="prism-ratio-frame"><div class="FvQLF iLTd NqeUA UzzHi iWsMV "><picture data-testid="prism-picture"><source media="(max-width: 767px)" srcSet="https://i.natgeofe.com/n/3b86ed4b-18d3-4ea7-8879-628fe30b6d5b/skeleton%20_square.jpg?w=195&amp;h=195, https://i.natgeofe.com/n/3b86ed4b-18d3-4ea7-8879-628fe30b6d5b/skeleton%20_square.jpg?w=390&amp;h=390 2x"/><source media="(min-width: 768px)" srcSet="https://i.natgeofe.com/n/3b86ed4b-18d3-4ea7-8879-628fe30b6d5b/skeleton%20_square.jpg?w=220&amp;h=220, https://i.natgeofe.com/n/3b86ed4b-18d3-4ea7-8879-628fe30b6d5b/skeleton%20_square.jpg?w=440&amp;h=440 2x"/><img alt="" class="hsDdd " data-testid="prism-image" draggable="false" src="https://i.natgeofe.com/n/3b86ed4b-18d3-4ea7-8879-628fe30b6d5b/skeleton%20_square.jpg"/></picture></div></div></div><div class="QGHKv iVcn avodi rEPuv ICwhc ibBnq Bkgbl ZLXw kSqqG rEBmF "><div class="VZTD rEPuv QXDKT pJYTK " data-testid="prism-meta"><div class="CJAFL gDeX "><div class="mLASH VZTD UeCOM wSnmx ltDkr MjHGf rmiAn vvBSK " id="Thismandrowned5000yetags"><div class="wXbPV YAJid wPGsL ">HISTORY &amp; CULTURE</div></div><h2 class="PFoxV eBpQD rcQBv bQtjQ lQUdN GpQCA mAkiF FvMyr WvoqU nPLLM tuAKv " id="Thismandrowned5000yeheadline">This man drowned 5,000 years ago. How do we know that?</h2></div></div></div></a></div><div class="liAe uMOq zYIfP pYgZk Mxrkk VZTD lZur TPpRg NoUSU igcMP DtJWr QgBvn DFdlJ QGHKv VuOFc EwJTR UpiKB sKbok RsAxh msYPt zKjNI SXHxp OaElp halTF KzevM LFuuA xTOeQ jLoop " data-testid="prism-card"><a class="iVcn UbGlr ibBnq qdXbA avodi DbOXS tqUtK GpWVU iJYzE QGHKv HNQqj ICwhc Bkgbl ZLXw kSqqG rEBmF " data-testid="prism-linkbase" href="https://www.nationalgeographic.com/history/article/maya-civilization-rural-collapse-controversy" aria-label="Why the idea that the Maya civilization ‘collapsed’ is wrong" aria-describedby="WhytheideathattheMaytags"><div class="hsDdd GpQCA lZur BOsoU YMZw dihEb srtah LmIPo JzlZQ qrShQ iRFVw ZZxEf zHngH jCA-DP TucPs XifJd MWLZF PEVz VbrfA zZsl kjmkg OwbFk QuuaM cBQOR "><div class="GpQCA lZur oVsVV nFtJ GHKp awJgN EuJtJ " data-testid="prism-ratio-frame"><div class="FvQLF iLTd NqeUA UzzHi iWsMV "><picture data-testid="prism-picture"><source media="(max-width: 767px)" srcSet="https://i.natgeofe.com/n/339fafe3-1bd9-4eed-b79a-8f68df6f020c/NationalGeographic_1574755_square.jpg?w=195&amp;h=195, https://i.natgeofe.com/n/339fafe3-1bd9-4eed-b79a-8f68df6f020c/NationalGeographic_1574755_square.jpg?w=390&amp;h=390 2x"/><source media="(min-width: 768px)" srcSet="https://i.natgeofe.com/n/339fafe3-1bd9-4eed-b79a-8f68df6f020c/NationalGeographic_1574755_square.jpg?w=220&amp;h=220, https://i.natgeofe.com/n/339fafe3-1bd9-4eed-b79a-8f68df6f020c/NationalGeographic_1574755_square.jpg?w=440&amp;h=440 2x"/><img alt="" class="hsDdd " data-testid="prism-image" draggable="false" src="https://i.natgeofe.com/n/339fafe3-1bd9-4eed-b79a-8f68df6f020c/NationalGeographic_1574755_square.jpg"/></picture></div></div></div><div class="QGHKv iVcn avodi rEPuv ICwhc ibBnq Bkgbl ZLXw kSqqG rEBmF "><div class="VZTD rEPuv QXDKT pJYTK " data-testid="prism-meta"><div class="CJAFL gDeX "><div class="mLASH VZTD UeCOM wSnmx ltDkr MjHGf rmiAn vvBSK " id="WhytheideathattheMaytags"><div class="wXbPV YAJid wPGsL ">HISTORY &amp; CULTURE</div></div><h2 class="PFoxV eBpQD rcQBv bQtjQ lQUdN GpQCA mAkiF FvMyr WvoqU nPLLM tuAKv " id="WhytheideathattheMayheadline">Why the idea that the Maya civilization ‘collapsed’ is wrong</h2></div></div></div></a></div></section></div><div class="XQpSH zzkIM UtCfs Ufjyt " data-testid="prism-divider"></div></div><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">“At that point we kind of looked at each other, and the supervisor of the area said, ‘I don’t think this is a modern trench. I think this is an ancient trench,’” Cline recalls. “And one of us said, ‘Um, earthquake?’ And we were like, Yeah, maybe. Let’s call Michael.”</p></div></div></div><div class="NYwzQ vUYNV glxIO ilAoG HPkGR "><div class="natgeo-ad" data-testid="prism-ad-wrapper" style="min-width:728px;min-height:90px;transition:min-height 0.3s linear 0s" data-ad-placeholder="true"><div data-box-type="fitt-adbox-fitt-article-inline-outstream" data-testid="prism-ad"><div class="Ad fitt-article-inline-outstream  ad-slot  " data-slot-type="fitt-article-inline-outstream" data-slot-kvps="pos=fitt-article-inline-outstream-2"></div></div></div></div><div class="FITT_Article_main_group_wrapper VZTD UeCOM jIRH oimqG DjbQm UwdmX Xmrlz ReShI KaJdY lqtkC ssImf HfYhe RTHNs iJVrZ " data-testid="prism-GridContainer"><div class="Kiog kNVGM nvpSA qwdi bmjsw " data-testid="prism-GridRow"><div class="theme-e oBTii mrzah " data-testid="prism-GridColumn" style="--grid-column-span-xxs:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-xs:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-sm:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-md:20;--grid-column-span-lg:16;--grid-column-span-xl:16;--grid-column-span-xxl:14;--grid-column-start-xxs:auto;--grid-column-start-xs:auto;--grid-column-start-sm:auto;--grid-column-start-md:3;--grid-column-start-lg:5;--grid-column-start-xl:5;--grid-column-start-xxl:6"><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy "><a class="zZygg UbGlr iFzkS qdXbA WCDhQ DbOXS tqUtK GpWVU iJYzE " data-testid="prism-linkbase" href="https://www.tau.ac.il/~zviba/MDSRC/staff/michael.html">Michael Lazar</a>, a research scientist at the University of Haifa’s department of marine geosciences and lead author of the <i class=" ">PLoS One</i> paper, had visited Tel Kabri in 2013 when the team first uncovered a storage room for wine. “I saw a bunch of jars that had been smashed by a roof collapse,” he recalls. “Assaf said, ‘What do you think?’ and I said, Earthquake. And Assaf said, ‘No, what really do you think caused it?’”</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Now, six years later, the experts stood around the trench and speculated that it was a fissure caused by an earthquake. Perhaps it was the result of liquefaction (when water-saturated soil loses its structure), either from a direct hit by an earthquake or a secondary result from a more distant earthquake that disturbed the high-water table at Tel Kabri.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">The researchers then started analyzing the fine grains of sediment that covered the palace floor and found that it was a chaotic tumble of plaster and broken wall, laid down in a single event. A lack of mud slurry showed that the floor was not exposed to the elements for any amount of time before the sediment layer covered it. This was an immediate event, not a slow decay.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Taken together, all the odd features began to make sense: the offset walls; the sloping, pockmarked floors; the enormous clay wine jars smashed in place; the microgeological evidence; and the fissure that split the palace in two. Adding to that, sediment records from the Dead Sea indicate that an earthquake occurred in the region around 1700 B.C., the time the palace was abandoned. An earthquake would be the only likely explanation.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">“This is archaeology,” says Cline. “You know, pieces come together. You discard hypotheses, you get more plausible hypotheses, and then eventually you have to invoke Sherlock Holmes, right? You eliminate the impossible and work with whatever’s left.”</p></div></div></div><div class="NYwzQ vUYNV glxIO ilAoG HPkGR "><div class="natgeo-ad" data-testid="prism-ad-wrapper" style="min-width:728px;min-height:90px;transition:min-height 0.3s linear 0s" data-ad-placeholder="true"><div data-box-type="fitt-adbox-fitt-article-inline-outstream" data-testid="prism-ad"><div class="Ad fitt-article-inline-outstream  ad-slot  " data-slot-type="fitt-article-inline-outstream" data-slot-kvps="pos=fitt-article-inline-outstream-3"></div></div></div></div><div class="FITT_Article_main_group_wrapper VZTD UeCOM jIRH oimqG DjbQm UwdmX Xmrlz ReShI KaJdY lqtkC ssImf HfYhe RTHNs iJVrZ " data-testid="prism-GridContainer"><div class="Kiog kNVGM nvpSA qwdi bmjsw " data-testid="prism-GridRow"><div class="theme-e oBTii mrzah " data-testid="prism-GridColumn" style="--grid-column-span-xxs:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-xs:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-sm:var(--grid-columns);--grid-column-span-md:20;--grid-column-span-lg:16;--grid-column-span-xl:16;--grid-column-span-xxl:14;--grid-column-start-xxs:auto;--grid-column-start-xs:auto;--grid-column-start-sm:auto;--grid-column-start-md:3;--grid-column-start-lg:5;--grid-column-start-xl:5;--grid-column-start-xxl:6"><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy "><a class="zZygg UbGlr iFzkS qdXbA WCDhQ DbOXS tqUtK GpWVU iJYzE " data-testid="prism-linkbase" href="https://cas.umkc.edu/directory/niemi-tina/">Tina Niemi</a>, a geologist at the University of Missouri-Kansas City who was not involved with the Tel Kabri project, agrees that the evidence seems to point to an earthquake, though she says more research is needed to determine exactly where it originated. Could it be the small Kabri fault, which runs near the site? Or the bigger and more dangerous Dead Sea fault, some 25 miles to the east? Excavating a cross section of the fissure that runs through the palace, she says, may help answer that question.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Yasur-Landau is no longer a skeptic when it comes to the earthquake hypothesis. “We’ve been working on the project for five years or so on this specific question, so it’s really, really gratifying that we have an answer.”</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">But for Lazar, the discovery raises new concerns for the residents of the area, particularly if the Kabri fault turns out to be the culprit for the palace’s destruction. “When you speak of earthquakes and Israel, everyone thinks of the Dead Sea fault,” he says. “That’s it, and that everything off the Dead Sea fault is not considered a major threat.”</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Lazar adds that the Kabri fault has been removed from the new map of potentially active faults in Israel. Yet if it was indeed responsible for the damage wrought just 3,700 years ago—a mere blip in geological time—its potential for future activity cannot be ruled out.</p><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">“It has definite meaning for hazard assessment, and we need to put it back on the map.”</p></div></div></div><div class="eTIW vUYNV glxIO ilAoG sUzSN "><div class="natgeo-ad" the 18th century B.C., a Canaanite palace at Tel Kabri, in what is today northern Israel, was a sight to behold. The enormous building—at 65,000 square feet it was larger than a modern shopping mall—was replete with wall paintings, a fancy banquet hall, and storage rooms packed with more than a hundred enormous jars of spiced wine."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html1","cntnt":{"mrkup":"Then, at some point during that century, the palace was suddenly abandoned and left vacant for almost a millennium."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html2","cntnt":{"mrkup":"Some 3,700 years later, beginning in 2009, archaeologists digging up the palace were stumped. This beautiful and important building obviously had served as a political center for Canaanites in the region. And it had been renovated shortly before it fell into disuse. So why did its inhabitants flee?"},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html3","cntnt":{"mrkup":"<i><a href=\"https://www.nationalgeographic.com/history/article/dna-from-biblical-canaanites-lives-modern-arabs-jews\">Read how DNA from the Bible's Canaanites lives on in modern Arabs and Jews.</a></i>"},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"inline-1","cntnt":{"cmsType":"image","ariaLabel":"image","align":"contentWidth","belowParagraph":true,"credit":"Photograph by Eric H. Cline","envNme":"prod","flags":{"hideTitle":true,"hideAssetSource":true},"qryStr":"userab=ng_pw_copy-287*variant_a-1126&forceMode=fitt","mrkup":"","placement":"inline"},"type":"inline","style":{}},{"id":"html4","cntnt":{"mrkup":"The 75-acre site of<a href=\"https://www.nationalgeographic.org/article/tel-kabri-project/\"> Tel Kabri</a> lies in a tectonically active region, so it would be easy to lay the blame on an earthquake. But the archaeologists were hesitant: Invoking an earthquake felt like an easy way out, like the joke among archaeologists of assigning a “ritual” purpose to artifacts they can’t otherwise explain."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html5","cntnt":{"mrkup":"Instead, the Tel Kabri team spent several dig seasons ruling out the possibilities. With support from the <a href=\"https://www.nationalgeographic.org/funding-opportunities/grants/\">National Geographic Society</a>, they looked for evidence of drought, flood, or other environmental factors that may have driven away the residents. They looked for signs of fire, weapons, or unburied bodies that may have indicated violence or combat. Nada. Zilch."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"inline-2","cntnt":{"cmsType":"image","ariaLabel":"image","align":"contentWidth","belowParagraph":true,"credit":"Photograph by Griffin Aerial Imaging","envNme":"prod","flags":{"hideTitle":true,"hideAssetSource":true},"qryStr":"userab=ng_pw_copy-287*variant_a-1126&forceMode=fitt","mrkup":"","placement":"inline"},"type":"inline","style":{}},{"id":"html6","cntnt":{"mrkup":"<a href=\"https://marsci.haifa.ac.il/index.php/en/staff/civi-faculty/168-ayasur\">Assaf Yasur Landau</a> of Haifa University, co-director of the excavation and a co-author of<a href=\"https://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0239079\"> a study published today</a> in the journal <i>PLoS One</i>, said it took him six years to warm to the idea that an earthquake may have destroyed the Canaanite palace."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html7","cntnt":{"mrkup":"“I wanted to make absolutely sure that we dotted every i and crossed every t before we reached such a conclusion,” he says. “It’s super important not to be sensationalist and to do good science. Otherwise it’s really bad for science, as well as for the community we serve.”"},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html8","cntnt":{"mrkup":"In 2011 the Tel Kabri team began uncovering a trench that appeared to cut straight through the palace. At first the archaeologists assumed it was modern, perhaps an irrigation channel for the avocado farm that surrounded the site, or maybe it was dug during the 1948 Arab-Israeli war."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html9","cntnt":{"mrkup":"“There was a battle in ’48 right across the road,” says Tel Kabri co-director<a href=\"https://anthropology.columbian.gwu.edu/eric-h-cline\"> Eric Cline</a> of George Washington University. “In our notes we were calling it a modern tank trench.”"},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html10","cntnt":{"mrkup":"Yet over the course of several excavation seasons, the archaeologists began to notice features in the palace that didn’t seem quite right. Some walls were slightly offset. Some floors were a little “wavy,” sloped at odd angles, or pockmarked, likely by heavy objects falling from a height."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html11","cntnt":{"mrkup":"By 2019, a hundred feet of the trench had been uncovered, and archaeologists noticed that three courses of a wall from the palace appeared to have fallen into the trench."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html12","cntnt":{"mrkup":"“At that point we kind of looked at each other, and the supervisor of the area said, ‘I don’t think this is a modern trench. I think this is an ancient trench,’” Cline recalls. “And one of us said, ‘Um, earthquake?’ And we were like, Yeah, maybe. Let’s call Michael.”"},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html13","cntnt":{"mrkup":"<a href=\"https://www.tau.ac.il/~zviba/MDSRC/staff/michael.html\">Michael Lazar</a>, a research scientist at the University of Haifa’s department of marine geosciences and lead author of the <i>PLoS One</i> paper, had visited Tel Kabri in 2013 when the team first uncovered a storage room for wine. “I saw a bunch of jars that had been smashed by a roof collapse,” he recalls. “Assaf said, ‘What do you think?’ and I said, Earthquake. And Assaf said, ‘No, what really do you think caused it?’”"},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html14","cntnt":{"mrkup":"Now, six years later, the experts stood around the trench and speculated that it was a fissure caused by an earthquake. Perhaps it was the result of liquefaction (when water-saturated soil loses its structure), either from a direct hit by an earthquake or a secondary result from a more distant earthquake that disturbed the high-water table at Tel Kabri."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html15","cntnt":{"mrkup":"The researchers then started analyzing the fine grains of sediment that covered the palace floor and found that it was a chaotic tumble of plaster and broken wall, laid down in a single event. A lack of mud slurry showed that the floor was not exposed to the elements for any amount of time before the sediment layer covered it. This was an immediate event, not a slow decay."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html16","cntnt":{"mrkup":"Taken together, all the odd features began to make sense: the offset walls; the sloping, pockmarked floors; the enormous clay wine jars smashed in place; the microgeological evidence; and the fissure that split the palace in two. Adding to that, sediment records from the Dead Sea indicate that an earthquake occurred in the region around 1700 B.C., the time the palace was abandoned. An earthquake would be the only likely explanation."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html17","cntnt":{"mrkup":"“This is archaeology,” says Cline. “You know, pieces come together. You discard hypotheses, you get more plausible hypotheses, and then eventually you have to invoke Sherlock Holmes, right? You eliminate the impossible and work with whatever’s left.”"},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html18","cntnt":{"mrkup":"<a href=\"https://cas.umkc.edu/directory/niemi-tina/\">Tina Niemi</a>, a geologist at the University of Missouri-Kansas City who was not involved with the Tel Kabri project, agrees that the evidence seems to point to an earthquake, though she says more research is needed to determine exactly where it originated. Could it be the small Kabri fault, which runs near the site? Or the bigger and more dangerous Dead Sea fault, some 25 miles to the east? Excavating a cross section of the fissure that runs through the palace, she says, may help answer that question."},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html19","cntnt":{"mrkup":"Yasur-Landau is no longer a skeptic when it comes to the earthquake hypothesis. “We’ve been working on the project for five years or so on this specific question, so it’s really, really gratifying that we have an answer.”"},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html20","cntnt":{"mrkup":"But for Lazar, the discovery raises new concerns for the residents of the area, particularly if the Kabri fault turns out to be the culprit for the palace’s destruction. “When you speak of earthquakes and Israel, everyone thinks of the Dead Sea fault,” he says. “That’s it, and that everything off the Dead Sea fault is not considered a major threat.”"},"type":"p","style":{}},{"id":"html21","cntnt":{"mrkup":"Lazar adds that the Kabri fault has been removed from the new map of potentially active faults in Israel. A lack of mud slurry showed that the floor was not exposed to the elements for any amount of time before the sediment layer covered it. This was an immediate event, not a slow decay."]},{"type":"p","content":["Taken together, all the odd features began to make sense: the offset walls; the sloping, pockmarked floors; the enormous clay wine jars smashed in place; the microgeological evidence; and the fissure that split the palace in two. Adding to that, sediment records from the Dead Sea indicate that an earthquake occurred in the region around 1700 B.C., the time the palace was abandoned. An earthquake would be the only likely explanation."]},{"type":"p","content":["“This is archaeology,” says Cline. “You know, pieces come together. You discard hypotheses, you get more plausible hypotheses, and then eventually you have to invoke Sherlock Holmes, right? You eliminate the impossible and work with whatever’s left.”"]}],{"type":"inline","content":{"name":"Ad","props":{"ad":{"kvps":{"pos":"fitt-article-inline-outstream-3"},"type":"fitt-article-inline-outstream","className":"fitt-article-inline-outstream"},"className":"natgeo-ad","placeholders":{"compact":{"size":[320,50]},"regular":{"size":[728,90]}},"initSelf":true},"context":{},"config":{"gridDisplayMode":"none"}}},[{"type":"p","content":[{"type":"a","content":["Tina Niemi"],"attrs":{"href":"https://cas.umkc.edu/directory/niemi-tina/"}},", a geologist at the University of Missouri-Kansas City who was not involved with the Tel Kabri project, agrees that the evidence seems to point to an earthquake, though she says more research is needed to determine exactly where it originated. Could it be the small Kabri fault, which runs near the site? Or the bigger and more dangerous Dead Sea fault, some 25 miles to the east? Excavating a cross section of the fissure that runs through the palace, she says, may help answer that question."]},{"type":"p","content":["Yasur-Landau is no longer a skeptic when it comes to the earthquake hypothesis. “We’ve been working on the project for five years or so on this specific question, so it’s really, really gratifying that we have an answer.”"]},{"type":"p","content":["But for Lazar, the discovery raises new concerns for the residents of the area, particularly if the Kabri fault turns out to be the culprit for the palace’s destruction. “When you speak of earthquakes and Israel, everyone thinks of the Dead Sea fault,” he says. “That’s it, and that everything off the Dead Sea fault is not considered a major threat.”"]},{"type":"p","content":["Lazar adds that the Kabri fault has been removed from the new map of potentially active faults in Israel.
